<p>One <a href="/wiki/Tablespoon" title="Tablespoon">tablespoon</a> of olive oil (13.5&#160;g) contains the following nutritional information according to the USDA:<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Calories: 119</li>
<li>Fat: 13.50&#160;g (21% of the <a href="/wiki/Daily_Value" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily Value">Daily Value</a>, DV)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saturated_fat" title="Saturated fat">Saturated fat</a>: 2&#160;g (9% of DV)</li>
<li>Carbohydrates: 0</li>
<li>Fibers: 0</li>
<li>Protein: 0</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vitamin_E" title="Vitamin E">Vitamin E</a>: 1.9&#160;mg (10% of DV)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vitamin_K" title="Vitamin K">Vitamin K</a>: 8.1&#160;µg (10% of DV)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Potential_health_effects:_fat_and_polyphenol_composition">Potential health effects: fat and polyphenol composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Olive_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Potential health effects: fat and polyphenol composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Olive oil consumption is thought to affect <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_health" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardiovascular health">cardiovascular health</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-schw_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schw-88">[87]</a></sup> It has been suggested that long-term consumption of small quantities of the <a href="/wiki/Polyphenol" title="Polyphenol">polyphenol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oleocanthal" title="Oleocanthal">oleocanthal</a>, from olive oil may be responsible in part for the low incidence of <a href="/wiki/Heart_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Heart disease">heart disease</a> associated with a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_diet" title="Mediterranean diet">Mediterranean diet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology" title="Epidemiology">Epidemiological studies</a> indicate that a higher proportion of <a href="/wiki/Monounsaturated_fat" title="Monounsaturated fat">monounsaturated fats</a> in the diet may be linked with a reduction in the risk of <a href="/wiki/Coronary_heart_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronary heart disease">coronary heart disease</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> There is preliminary evidence that regular consumption of olive oil may lower risk of all-cause mortality and several chronic diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-schw_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schw-88">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BucklandGonzalez2015_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BucklandGonzalez2015-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a comprehensive scientific review by the <a href="/wiki/European_Food_Safety_Authority" title="European Food Safety Authority">European Food Safety Authority</a> (EFSA) in 2011, health claims on olive oil were approved for protection by its <a href="/wiki/Polyphenol" title="Polyphenol">polyphenols</a> against <a href="/wiki/Oxidation" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxidation">oxidation</a> of blood lipids,<sup id="cite_ref-EFSApolyphenols2011_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EFSApolyphenols2011-92">[91]</a></sup> and for the contribution to the maintenance of normal blood <a href="/wiki/LDL-cholesterol" class="mw-redirect" title="LDL-cholesterol">LDL-cholesterol</a> levels by replacing saturated fats in the diet with <a href="/wiki/Oleic_acid" title="Oleic acid">oleic acid</a><sup id="cite_ref-EFSAoleicacid2011_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EFSAoleicacid2011-93">[92]</a></sup> (Commission Regulation (EU) 432/2012 of 16 May 2012).<sup id="cite_ref-OfficialJournalEuropeanUnion2012_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OfficialJournalEuropeanUnion2012-94">[93]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Cause-and-effect" class="mw-redirect" title="Cause-and-effect">cause-and-effect</a> relationship has not been adequately established for consumption of olive oil and maintaining normal (fasting) blood concentrations of <a href="/wiki/Triglycerides" class="mw-redirect" title="Triglycerides">triglycerides</a>, normal blood <a href="/wiki/HDL-cholesterol" class="mw-redirect" title="HDL-cholesterol">HDL-cholesterol</a> concentrations, and normal <a href="/wiki/Blood_glucose" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood glucose">blood glucose</a> concentrations.<sup id="cite_ref-EFSA_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EFSA-95">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 2011 meta-analysis concluded that olive oil consumption may play a protective role against the development of any type of cancer, but could not clarify whether the beneficial effect is due to olive oil monounsaturated fatty acid content or its antioxidant components.<sup id="cite_ref-PsaltopoulouKosti2011_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PsaltopoulouKosti2011-96">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 2014 meta-analysis concluded that an elevated consumption of olive oil is associated with reduced risk of all-cause mortality, cardiovascular events and stroke, while monounsaturated fatty acids of mixed animal and plant origin showed no significant effects.<sup id="cite_ref-SchwingshacklHoffmann2014_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SchwingshacklHoffmann2014-97">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United States, producers of olive oil may place the following restricted health claim on product labels:</p>
<dl>
<dd>Limited and not conclusive scientific evidence suggests that eating about 2&#160;<a href="/wiki/Tablespoon" title="Tablespoon">tbsp.</a> (23&#160;g) of olive oil daily may reduce the risk of coronary heart disease due to the monounsaturated fat in olive oil. To achieve this possible benefit, olive oil is to replace a similar amount of <a href="/wiki/Saturated_fat" title="Saturated fat">saturated fat</a> and not increase the total number of calories you eat in a day.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p>This decision was announced November 1, 2004 after application to the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">FDA</a> by producers.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> Similar labels are permitted for foods rich in <a href="/wiki/Omega-3_fatty_acid" title="Omega-3 fatty acid">omega-3 fatty acids</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Walnut" title="Walnut">walnuts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hemp" title="Hemp">hemp</a> seed.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Olive_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">
<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Foodlogo2.svg" class="image"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Foodlogo2.svg/32px-Foodlogo2.svg.png" width="32" height="23" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Foodlogo2.svg/48px-Foodlogo2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Foodlogo2.svg/64px-Foodlogo2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="146" data-file-height="106" /></a></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Food" title="Portal:Food">Food portal</a></span></li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Olive_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> word for <i>olive oil</i> or for <i><a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a></i> in general, <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">ἔλαιον</span> (<i>elaion</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> is first attested in the <a href="/wiki/Mycenaean_Greek" title="Mycenaean Greek">Mycenaean Greek</a> forms <span lang="gmy" xml:lang="gmy">𐀁𐀨𐀺</span>, <i>e-ra-wo</i> and <span lang="gmy" xml:lang="gmy">𐀁𐁉𐀺</span>, <i>e-rai-wo</i>, written in the <a href="/wiki/Linear_B" title="Linear B">Linear B</a> <a href="/wiki/Syllabic_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Syllabic script">syllabic script</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In Linear B there was also <span lang="gmy" xml:lang="gmy">𐂕</span>, an <a href="/wiki/Ideogram" title="Ideogram">ideogram</a> standing for <i>olive oil</i> or <i>oil</i> in general.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>

Harris (December 2011) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://olivecenter.ucdavis.edu/files/microbial%20safety%20120511.pdf">"Microbiological Food Safety of Olive Oil: A Review of the Literature"</a> (PDF), <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis" title="University of California, Davis">University of California, Davis</a></li>
<li>Preedy, V.R. / Watson, R.R. (eds.). <i>Olives and Olive Oil in Health and Disease Prevention</i>, Academic Press, 2010. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780123744203" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-12-374420-3</a>.</li>
<li>Rosenblum, Mort. <i>Olives: The Life and Lore of a Noble Fruit</i>, North Point Press, 1996. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0865475032" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0-86547-503-2</a>.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.codexalimentarius.org/download/standards/88/CXS_033e.pdf">CODEX STAN 33-1981 Standard for Olive Oils and Olive Pomace Oils</a></li>
</ul>
